class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cleveland_Indians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 1994: Jacobs Field opens">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1994_Cleveland_Indians_season" title="1994 Cleveland Indians season">1994 Cleveland Indians season</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Progressive_Field.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Progressive_Field.jpg/220px-Progressive_Field.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Progressive_Field.jpg/330px-Progressive_Field.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Progressive_Field.jpg/440px-Progressive_Field.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Progressive_Field.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Progressive_Field" title="Progressive Field">Progressive Field</a> in 2008</div></div></div>\n<p>Indians General Manager <a href="/wiki/John_Hart_(baseball)" title="John Hart (baseball)">John Hart</a> and team owner <a href="/wiki/Richard_Jacobs_(businessman)" title="Richard Jacobs (businessman)">Richard Jacobs</a> managed to turn the team\'s fortunes around. The Indians opened <a href="/wiki/Jacobs_Field" class="mw-redirect" title="Jacobs Field">Jacobs Field</a> in <a href="/wiki/1994_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1994 Major League Baseball season">1994</a> with the aim of improving on the prior season\'s sixth-place finish. The Indians were only one game behind the division-leading <a href="/wiki/1994_Chicago_White_Sox_season" title="1994 Chicago White Sox season">Chicago White Sox</a> on August 12 when a <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_Major_League_Baseball_strike" title="1994\xe2\x80\x9395 Major League Baseball strike">players strike</a> wiped out the rest of the season.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1995:_First_AL_pennant_since_1954">1995: First AL pennant since 1954</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cleveland_Indians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 1995: First AL pennant since 1954">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1995_Cleveland_Indians_season" title="1995 Cleveland Indians season">1995 Cleveland Indians season</a></div>\n<p>Having contended for the division in the aborted 1994 season, Cleveland sprinted to a 100\xe2\x80\x9344 record (the season was shortened by 18 games due to player/owner negotiations) in 1995, winning its first ever divisional title. Veterans <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Mart%C3%ADnez" title="Dennis Mart\xc3\xadnez">Dennis Mart\xc3\xadnez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orel_Hershiser" title="Orel Hershiser">Orel Hershiser</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Murray" title="Eddie Murray">Eddie Murray</a> combined with a young core of players including <a href="/wiki/Omar_Vizquel" title="Omar Vizquel">Omar Vizquel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albert_Belle" title="Albert Belle">Albert Belle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Thome" title="Jim Thome">Jim Thome</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manny_Ram%C3%ADrez" class="mw-redirect" title="Manny Ram\xc3\xadrez">Manny Ram\xc3\xadrez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Lofton" title="Kenny Lofton">Kenny Lofton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charles_Nagy" title="Charles Nagy">Charles Nagy</a> to lead the league in team batting average as well as team ERA.\n</p><p>After defeating the <a href="/wiki/1995_Boston_Red_Sox_season" title="1995 Boston Red Sox season">Boston Red Sox</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1995_American_League_Division_Series" title="1995 American League Division Series">Division Series</a> and the <a href="/wiki/1995_Seattle_Mariners_season" title="1995 Seattle Mariners season">Seattle Mariners</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1995_American_League_Championship_Series" title="1995 American League Championship Series">ALCS</a>, Cleveland clinched the American League pennant and a <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a> berth, for the first time since 1954. The <a href="/wiki/1995_World_Series" title="1995 World Series">World Series</a> ended in disappointment with the Indians falling in six games to the <a href="/wiki/1995_Atlanta_Braves_season" title="1995 Atlanta Braves season">Atlanta Braves</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1996">1996</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cleveland_Indians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: 1996">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1996_Cleveland_Indians_season" title="1996 Cleveland Indians season">1996 Cleveland Indians season</a></div>\n<p>Tickets for every Indians home game sold out several months before opening day in <a href="/wiki/1996_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1996 Major League Baseball season">1996</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Tickets_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tickets-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The Indians repeated as AL Central champions but lost to the <a href="/wiki/1996_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1996 Baltimore Orioles season">Baltimore Orioles</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1996_American_League_Division_Series" title="1996 American League Division Series">Division Series</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1997:_One_inning_away">1997: One inning away</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cleveland_Indians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: 1997: One inning away">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1997_Cleveland_Indians_season" title="1997 Cleveland Indians season">1997 Cleveland Indians season</a></div>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/1997_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1997 Major League Baseball season">1997</a> Cleveland started slow but finished with an 86\xe2\x80\x9375 record. Taking their third consecutive AL Central title, the Indians defeated the <a href="/wiki/1997_New_York_Yankees_season" title="1997 New York Yankees season">New York Yankees</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1997_American_League_Division_Series" title="1997 American League Division Series">Division Series</a>, 3\xe2\x80\x932. After defeating the <a href="/wiki/1997_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1997 Baltimore Orioles season">Baltimore Orioles</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1997_American_League_Championship_Series" title="1997 American League Championship Series">ALCS</a>, Cleveland went on to face the <a href="/wiki/1997_Florida_Marlins_season" title="1997 Florida Marlins season">Florida Marlins</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1997_World_Series" title="1997 World Series">World Series</a> which featured the coldest game in World Series history. With the series tied after Game 6, the Indians went into the ninth inning of Game Seven with a 2\xe2\x80\x931 lead, but closer <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mesa" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Mesa">Jos\xc3\xa9 Mesa</a> allowed the Marlins to tie the game. In the eleventh inning, <a href="/wiki/%C3%89dgar_Renter%C3%ADa" title="\xc3\x89dgar Renter\xc3\xada">\xc3\x89dgar Renter\xc3\xada</a> drove in the winning run giving the Marlins their first championship.  Cleveland became the first team to lose the World Series after carrying the lead into the ninth inning of the seventh game.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="1998.E2.80.932001"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1998\xe2\x80\x932001">1998\xe2\x80\x932001</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cleveland_Indians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: 1998\xe2\x80\x932001">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/1998_Cleveland_Indians_season" title="1998 Cleveland Indians season">1998</a>, the Indians made the postseason for the fourth straight year. After defeating the wild-card <a href="/wiki/1998_Boston_Red_Sox_season" title="1998 Boston Red Sox season">Boston Red Sox</a> 3\xe2\x80\x931 in the <a href="/wiki/1998_American_League_Division_Series" title="1998 American League Division Series">Division Series</a>, Cleveland lost the <a href="/wiki/1998_American_League_Championship_Series" title="1998 American League Championship Series">1998 ALCS</a> in six games to the <a href="/wiki/1998_New_York_Yankees_season" title="1998 New York Yankees season">New York Yankees</a>, who had come into the postseason with a then-AL record 114 wins in the regular season.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>For the <a href="/wiki/1999_Cleveland_Indians_season" title="1999 Cleveland Indians season">1999</a> season, Cleveland added relief pitcher <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Rinc%C3%B3n" title="Ricardo Rinc\xc3\xb3n">Ricardo Rinc\xc3\xb3n</a> and second baseman <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Alomar" title="Roberto Alomar">Roberto Alomar</a>, brother of catcher Sandy Alomar, Jr,<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> and won the Central Division title for the fifth consecutive year. The team scored 1,009 runs, becoming the first (and to date only) team since the 1950 Boston Red Sox to score more than 1,000 runs in a season. This time, Cleveland did not make it past the first round, losing the <a href="/wiki/1999_American_League_Division_Series" title="1999 American League Division Series">Division Series</a> to the <a href="/wiki/1999_Boston_Red_Sox_season" title="1999 Boston Red Sox season">Red Sox</a>, despite taking a 2\xe2\x80\x930 lead in the series. In game three, Indians starter Dave Burba went down with an injury in the 4th inning.<sup id="cite_ref-Burba_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Burba-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>  Four pitchers, including presumed game four starter <a href="/wiki/Jaret_Wright" title="Jaret Wright">Jaret Wright</a>, surrendered nine runs in relief. Without a long reliever or emergency starter on the playoff roster, Hargrove started both <a href="/wiki/Bartolo_Col%C3%B3n" title="Bartolo Col\xc3\xb3n">Bartolo Col\xc3\xb3n</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charles_Nagy" title="Charles Nagy">Charles Nagy</a> in games four and five on only three days rest.<sup id="cite_ref-Burba_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Burba-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>  The Indians lost game four 23\xe2\x80\x937 and game five 12\xe2\x80\x938.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>  Four days later, Hargrove was dismissed as manager.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/2000_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="2000 Major League Baseball season">2000</a>, the <a href="/wiki/2000_Cleveland_Indians_season" title="2000 Cleveland Indians season">Indians</a> had a 44\xe2\x80\x9342 start, but caught fire after the All Star break and went 46\xe2\x80\x9330 the rest of the way to finish 90\xe2\x80\x9372.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> The team had one of the league\'s best offenses that year and a defense that yielded three gold gloves. However, they ended up five games behind the <a href="/wiki/2000_Chicago_White_Sox_season" title="2000 Chicago White Sox season">Chicago White Sox</a> in the Central division and missed the wild card by one game to the <a href="/wiki/2000_Seattle_Mariners_season" title="2000 Seattle Mariners season">Seattle Mariners</a>. Mid-season trades brought <a href="/wiki/Bob_Wickman" title="Bob Wickman">Bob Wickman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jake_Westbrook" title="Jake Westbrook">Jake Westbrook</a> to Cleveland.  After the season and free agent outfielder <a href="/wiki/Manny_Ram%C3%ADrez" class="mw-redirect" title="Manny Ram\xc3\xadrez">Manny Ram\xc3\xadrez</a> departed for the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a>.\n</p><p>In 2000, <a href="/wiki/Larry_Dolan" title="Larry Dolan">Larry Dolan</a> bought the Indians for $320 million from Richard Jacobs, who, along with his late brother David, had paid $45 million for the club in 1986. The sale set a record at the time for the sale of a baseball franchise.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/2001_Cleveland_Indians_season" title="2001 Cleveland Indians season">2001</a> saw a return to the postseason. After the departures of Ram\xc3\xadrez and <a href="/wiki/Sandy_Alomar,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Sandy Alomar, Jr.">Sandy Alomar, Jr.</a>, the Indians signed Ellis Burks and former <a href="/wiki/MLB_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="MLB Most Valuable Player Award">MVP</a> <a href="/wiki/Juan_Gonz%C3%A1lez_(baseball)" title="Juan Gonz\xc3\xa1lez (baseball)">Juan Gonz\xc3\xa1lez</a>, who helped the team win the Central division with a 91\xe2\x80\x9371 record.  One of the highlights came on August 5, when the Indians completed the biggest comeback in MLB History. Cleveland rallied to close a 14\xe2\x80\x932 deficit in the seventh inning to defeat the <a href="/wiki/2001_Seattle_Mariners_season" title="2001 Seattle Mariners season">Seattle Mariners</a> 15\xe2\x80\x9314 in 11 innings. The Mariners, who won a MLB record-tying 116 games that season, had a strong bullpen, and Indians manager <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Manuel" title="Charlie Manuel">Charlie Manuel</a> had already pulled many of his starters with the game seemingly out of reach.\n</p><p>Seattle and Cleveland met in the <a href="/wiki/2001_American_League_Division_Series" title="2001 American League Division Series">first round of the postseason</a>, however the Mariners won the series 3\xe2\x80\x932. In the 2001\xe2\x80\x9302 offseason, GM John Hart resigned and his assistant, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Shapiro_(sports_executive)" title="Mark Shapiro (sports executive)">Mark Shapiro</a>, took the reins.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="2002.E2.80.9310:_The_Shapiro.2FWedge_years"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2002\xe2\x80\x9310:_The_Shapiro/Wedge_years">2002\xe2\x80\x9310: The Shapiro/Wedge years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cleveland_Indians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: 2002\xe2\x80\x9310: The Shapiro/Wedge years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mark_Shapiro.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Mark_Shapiro.png/170px-Mark_Shapiro.png" width="170" height="264" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ab/Mark_Shapiro.png 1.5x" data-file-width="216" data-file-height="336" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mark_Shapiro.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mark_Shapiro_(sports_executive)" title="Mark Shapiro (sports executive)">Mark Shapiro</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Indians GM from 2001\xe2\x80\x932010,  President from 2010\xe2\x80\x932015, and two-time <a href="/wiki/Sporting_News_Executive_of_the_Year_Award" title="Sporting News Executive of the Year Award">Sporting News Executive of the Year</a>.</div></div></div>\n<h4><span id="First_.22rebuilding_of_the_team.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="First_&quot;rebuilding_of_the_team&quot;">First "rebuilding of the team"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cleveland_Indians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: First &quot;rebuilding of the team&quot;">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Shapiro moved to rebuild by dealing aging veterans for younger talent. He traded <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Alomar" title="Roberto Alomar">Roberto Alomar</a> to the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a> for a package that included outfielder <a href="/wiki/Matt_Lawton" title="Matt Lawton">Matt Lawton</a> and prospects <a href="/wiki/Alex_Escobar" title="Alex Escobar">Alex Escobar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Billy_Traber" title="Billy Traber">Billy Traber</a>. When the team fell out of contention in mid-<a href="/wiki/2002_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="2002 Major League Baseball season">2002</a>, Shapiro fired manager <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Manuel" title="Charlie Manuel">Charlie Manuel</a> and traded pitching ace <a href="/wiki/Bartolo_Col%C3%B3n" title="Bartolo Col\xc3\xb3n">Bartolo Col\xc3\xb3n</a> for prospects <a href="/wiki/Brandon_Phillips" title="Brandon Phillips">Brandon Phillips</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cliff_Lee" title="Cliff Lee">Cliff Lee</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Grady_Sizemore" title="Grady Sizemore">Grady Sizemore</a>; acquired <a href="/wiki/Travis_Hafner" title="Travis Hafner">Travis Hafner</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Rangers_(baseball)" title="Texas Rangers (baseball)">Rangers</a> for <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Drese" title="Ryan Drese">Ryan Drese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Einar_D%C3%ADaz" title="Einar D\xc3\xadaz">Einar D\xc3\xadaz</a>; and picked up <a href="/wiki/Coco_Crisp" title="Coco Crisp">Coco Crisp</a> from the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a> for aging starter <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Finley" title="Chuck Finley">Chuck Finley</a>. <a href="/wiki/Jim_Thome" title="Jim Thome">Jim Thome</a> left after the season, going to the Phillies for a larger contract.\n</p><p>Young Indians teams finished far out of contention in 2002 and <a href="/wiki/2003_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="2003 Major League Baseball season">2003</a> under new manager <a href="/wiki/Eric_Wedge" title="Eric Wedge">Eric Wedge</a>. They posted strong offensive numbers in <a href="/wiki/2004_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="2004 Major League Baseball season">2004</a>, but continued to struggle with a bullpen that blew more than 20 saves. A highlight of the season was a 22\xe2\x80\x930 victory over the <a href="/wiki/2004_New_York_Yankees_season" title="2004 New York Yankees season">New York Yankees</a> on August 31, one of the worst defeats suffered by the Yankees in team history.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In early <a href="/wiki/2005_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="2005 Major League Baseball season">2005</a>, the offense got off to a poor start. After a brief July slump, the <a href="/wiki/2005_Cleveland_Indians_season" title="2005 Cleveland Indians season">Indians</a> caught fire in August, and cut a 15.5 game deficit in the Central Division down to 1.5 games. However, the season came to an end as the Indians went on to lose six of their last seven games, five of them by one run, missing the playoffs by only two games. Shapiro was named <a href="/wiki/Sporting_News_Executive_of_the_Year_Award" title="Sporting News Executive of the Year Award">Executive of the Year</a> in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-cleveland.com_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cleveland.com-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/2006_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="2006 Major League Baseball season">The next season</a>, the club made several roster changes, while retaining its nucleus of young players. The off-season was highlighted by the acquisition of top prospect <a href="/wiki/Andy_Marte" title="Andy Marte">Andy Marte</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a>.  The Indians had a solid offensive season, led by career years from <a href="/wiki/Travis_Hafner" title="Travis Hafner">Travis Hafner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grady_Sizemore" title="Grady Sizemore">Grady Sizemore</a>. Hafner, despite missing the last month of the season, tied the single season grand slam record of six, which was set in <a href="/wiki/1987_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1987 Major League Baseball season">1987</a> by <a href="/wiki/Don_Mattingly" title="Don Mattingly">Don Mattingly</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Despite the solid offensive performance, the bullpen struggled with 23 blown saves (a Major League worst), and the Indians finished a disappointing fourth.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/2007_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="2007 Major League Baseball season">2007</a>, Shapiro signed veteran help for the bullpen and outfield in the offseason. Veterans <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Fultz" title="Aaron Fultz">Aaron Fultz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joe_Borowski_(baseball)" title="Joe Borowski (baseball)">Joe Borowski</a> joined <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Betancourt" title="Rafael Betancourt">Rafael Betancourt</a> in the Indians bullpen.<sup id="cite_ref-MLB2007_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MLB2007-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> The Indians improved significantly over the prior year and went into the All-Star break in second place. The team brought back <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Lofton" title="Kenny Lofton">Kenny Lofton</a> for his third stint with the team in late July.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The Indians finished with a 96\xe2\x80\x9366 record tied with the Red Sox for best in baseball, their seventh Central Division title in 13 years and their first postseason trip since 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-WP2007_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WP2007-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:174px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CC_Sabathia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/CC_Sabathia.jpg/172px-CC_Sabathia.jpg" width="172" height="217" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/CC_Sabathia.jpg/258px-CC_Sabathia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/CC_Sabathia.jpg/344px-CC_Sabathia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1489" data-file-height="1881" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CC_Sabathia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/CC_Sabathia" title="CC Sabathia">CC Sabathia</a> \xe2\x80\x93 who won the 2007 A.L. <a href="/wiki/Cy_Young_Award" title="Cy Young Award">Cy Young Award</a> with the Indians, and was the first of back-to-back Indians Cy Young winners (with teammate <a href="/wiki/Cliff_Lee" title="Cliff Lee">Cliff Lee</a> winning the following year).</div></div></div>\n<p>The Indians began their playoff run by defeating the <a href="/wiki/2007_New_York_Yankees_season" title="2007 New York Yankees season">Yankees</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2007_American_League_Division_Series" title="2007 American League Division Series">ALDS</a> three games to one. This series will be most remembered for the swarm of bugs that overtook the field in the later innings of Game Two. They also jumped out to a three-games-to-one lead over the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Red Sox</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2007_American_League_Championship_Series" title="2007 American League Championship Series">ALCS</a>. The season ended in disappointment when Boston swept the final three games to advance to the <a href="/wiki/2007_World_Series" title="2007 World Series">2007 World Series</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WP2007_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WP2007-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Despite the loss, Cleveland players took home a number of awards. <a href="/wiki/Grady_Sizemore" title="Grady Sizemore">Grady Sizemore</a>, who had a .995 <a href="/wiki/Fielding_percentage" title="Fielding percentage">fielding percentage</a> and only two errors in 405 chances, won the <a href="/wiki/Rawlings_Gold_Glove_Award" title="Rawlings Gold Glove Award">Gold Glove award</a>, Cleveland\'s first since 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Indians Pitcher <a href="/wiki/CC_Sabathia" title="CC Sabathia">CC Sabathia</a> won the second <a href="/wiki/Cy_Young_Award" title="Cy Young Award">Cy Young Award</a> in team history with a 19\xe2\x80\x937 record, a 3.21 ERA and an MLB-leading 241 <a href="/wiki/Innings_pitched" title="Innings pitched">innings pitched</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> Eric Wedge was awarded the first <a href="/wiki/Manager_of_the_Year_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Manager of the Year Award">Manager of the Year Award</a> in team history.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Shapiro was named to his second <a href="/wiki/Sporting_News_Executive_of_the_Year_Award" title="Sporting News Executive of the Year Award">Executive of the Year</a> in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-cleveland.com_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cleveland.com-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Second_.22rebuilding_of_the_team.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_&quot;rebuilding_of_the_team&quot;">Second "rebuilding of the team"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cleveland_Indians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Second &quot;rebuilding of the team&quot;">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/2008_Cleveland_Indians_season" title="2008 Cleveland Indians season">Indians</a> struggled during the <a href="/wiki/2008_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="2008 Major League Baseball season">2008 season</a>.  Injuries to sluggers <a href="/wiki/Travis_Hafner" title="Travis Hafner">Travis Hafner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Victor_Martinez_(baseball)" class="mw-redirect" title="Victor Martinez (baseball)">Victor Martinez</a>, as well as starting pitchers <a href="/wiki/Jake_Westbrook" title="Jake Westbrook">Jake Westbrook</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fausto_Carmona" class="mw-redirect" title="Fausto Carmona">Fausto Carmona</a> led to a poor start.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>  The Indians, falling to last place for a short time in June and July, traded <a href="/wiki/CC_Sabathia" title="CC Sabathia">CC Sabathia</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee_Brewers" title="Milwaukee Brewers">Milwaukee Brewers</a> for prospects Matt LaPorta, Rob Bryson, and Michael Brantley.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> and traded starting third baseman Casey Blake for catching prospect Carlos Santana.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>  Pitcher <a href="/wiki/Cliff_Lee" title="Cliff Lee">Cliff Lee</a> went 22\xe2\x80\x933 with an ERA of 2.54 and earned the AL Cy Young Award.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Grady_Sizemore" title="Grady Sizemore">Grady Sizemore</a> had a career year, winning a <a href="/wiki/Gold_Glove_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Gold Glove Award">Gold Glove Award</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Silver_Slugger_Award" title="Silver Slugger Award">Silver Slugger Award</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> and the Indians finished with a record of 81\xe2\x80\x9381.\n</p><p>Prospects for the <a href="/wiki/2009_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="2009 Major League Baseball season">season</a> dimmed early when the <a href="/wiki/2009_Cleveland_Indians_season" title="2009 Cleveland Indians season">Indians</a> ended May with a record of 22\xe2\x80\x9330. Shapiro made multiple trades: <a href="/wiki/Cliff_Lee" title="Cliff Lee">Cliff Lee</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ben_Francisco" title="Ben Francisco">Ben Francisco</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Phillies" title="Philadelphia Phillies">Philadelphia Phillies</a> for prospects <a href="/wiki/Jason_Knapp_(baseball)" title="Jason Knapp (baseball)">Jason Knapp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Carrasco_(baseball)" title="Carlos Carrasco (baseball)">Carlos Carrasco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jason_Donald_(baseball)" title="Jason Donald (baseball)">Jason Donald</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lou_Marson" title="Lou Marson">Lou Marson</a>; <a href="/wiki/V%C3%ADctor_Mart%C3%ADnez_(baseball)" title="V\xc3\xadctor Mart\xc3\xadnez (baseball)">Victor Martinez</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a> for prospects <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Price" title="Bryan Price">Bryan Price</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nick_Hagadone" title="Nick Hagadone">Nick Hagadone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Justin_Masterson" title="Justin Masterson">Justin Masterson</a>; <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Garko" title="Ryan Garko">Ryan Garko</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Rangers_(baseball)" title="Texas Rangers (baseball)">Texas Rangers</a> for <a href="/wiki/Scott_Barnes_(baseball)" title="Scott Barnes (baseball)">Scott Barnes</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Shoppach" title="Kelly Shoppach">Kelly Shoppach</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Rays" title="Tampa Bay Rays">Tampa Bay Rays</a> for <a href="/wiki/Mitch_Talbot" title="Mitch Talbot">Mitch Talbot</a>. The Indians finished the season tied for fourth in their division, with a record of 65\xe2\x80\x9397. The team announced on September 30, 2009, that Eric Wedge and all of the team\'s coaching staff would be released at the end of the 2009 season.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Manny_Acta" title="Manny Acta">Manny Acta</a> was hired as the team\'s 40th manager on October 25, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On February 18, 2010, it was announced that Shapiro (following the end of the 2010 season) would be promoted to team President, with current President <a href="/wiki/Paul_Dolan_(baseball)" title="Paul Dolan (baseball)">Paul Dolan</a> becoming the new Chairman/CEO, and longtime Shapiro assistant <a href="/wiki/Chris_Antonetti" title="Chris Antonetti">Chris Antonetti</a> filling the GM role.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="2011.E2.80.93present:_Antonetti.2FFrancona_era"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2011\xe2\x80\x93present:_Antonetti/Francona_era">2011\xe2\x80\x93present: Antonetti/Francona era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cleveland_Indians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: 2011\xe2\x80\x93present: Antonetti/Francona era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Terry_Francona_on_June_26,_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Terry_Francona_on_June_26%2C_2013.jpg/170px-Terry_Francona_on_June_26%2C_2013.jpg" width="170" height="283" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Terry_Francona_on_June_26%2C_2013.jpg/255px-Terry_Francona_on_June_26%2C_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Terry_Francona_on_June_26%2C_2013.jpg/340px-Terry_Francona_on_June_26%2C_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1210" data-file-height="2017" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Terry_Francona_on_June_26,_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Two-time <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Terry_Francona" title="Terry Francona">Terry Francona</a>, who became Indians manager on October 6, 2012<br />In his tenure with the Tribe, he is a two-time AL Manager of the Year (2013, 2016) and led the team to the 2016 AL Championship.</div></div></div>\n<p>On January 18, 2011, longtime popular former first baseman and manager <a href="/wiki/Mike_Hargrove" title="Mike Hargrove">Mike Hargrove</a> was brought in as a special adviser. The Indians started the <a href="/wiki/2011_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="2011 Major League Baseball season">2011 season</a> strong&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 going 30\xe2\x80\x9315 in their first 45 games and seven games ahead of the <a href="/wiki/2011_Detroit_Tigers_season" title="2011 Detroit Tigers season">Detroit Tigers</a> for first place. Injuries led to a slump where the Indians fell out of first place. Many minor leaguers such as <a href="/wiki/Jason_Kipnis" title="Jason Kipnis">Jason Kipnis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lonnie_Chisenhall" title="Lonnie Chisenhall">Lonnie Chisenhall</a> got opportunities to fill in for the injuries.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> The biggest news of the season came on July 30 when the Indians traded four prospects for <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Rockies" title="Colorado Rockies">Colorado Rockies</a> star pitcher, <a href="/wiki/Ubaldo_Jim%C3%A9nez" title="Ubaldo Jim\xc3\xa9nez">Ubaldo Jim\xc3\xa9nez</a>. The Indians sent their top two pitchers in the minors, <a href="/wiki/Alex_White_(baseball)" title="Alex White (baseball)">Alex White</a> and <a href="/wiki/Drew_Pomeranz" title="Drew Pomeranz">Drew Pomeranz</a> along with <a href="/wiki/Joe_Gardner" title="Joe Gardner">Joe Gardner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Matt_McBride" title="Matt McBride">Matt McBride</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> On August 25, the Indians signed the team leader in home runs, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Thome" title="Jim Thome">Jim Thome</a> off of waivers.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> He made his first appearance in an Indians uniform since he left Cleveland after the 2002 season. To honor Thome, the Indians placed him at his original position, third base, for one pitch against the Minnesota Twins on September 25. It was his first time playing third base since 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> This would also be his last appearance as an Indian. The Indians finished the season in 2nd place, 15 games behind the division champion Tigers.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Corey_Kluber_on_June_27,_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Corey_Kluber_on_June_27%2C_2013.jpg/175px-Corey_Kluber_on_June_27%2C_2013.jpg" width="175" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Corey_Kluber_on_June_27%2C_2013.jpg/263px-Corey_Kluber_on_June_27%2C_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Corey_Kluber_on_June_27%2C_2013.jpg/350px-Corey_Kluber_on_June_27%2C_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1850" data-file-height="1850" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Corey_Kluber_on_June_27,_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Corey_Kluber" title="Corey Kluber">Corey Kluber</a> \xe2\x80\x93 who is a two-time AL <a href="/wiki/Cy_Young_Award" title="Cy Young Award">Cy Young Award</a> winner with the Indians (2014, 2017) -  giving the team four winners over 11 seasons.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Indians broke the Opening Day attendance record for <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Field" title="Progressive Field">Progressive Field</a> with 43,190 against the <a href="/wiki/2012_Toronto_Blue_Jays_season" title="2012 Toronto Blue Jays season">Toronto Blue Jays</a> on April 5, 2012. The game went on to be the longest opening day game by innings in MLB history. The game was 16 innings and lasted 5 hours and 14 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On September 27, 2012, with six games left in the Indians\' 2012 season, <a href="/wiki/Manny_Acta" title="Manny Acta">Manny Acta</a> was fired; <a href="/wiki/Sandy_Alomar,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Sandy Alomar, Jr.">Sandy Alomar, Jr.</a> was named interim manager for the remainder of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>  On October 6, the Indians announced that <a href="/wiki/Terry_Francona" title="Terry Francona">Terry Francona</a>, who managed the Boston Red Sox between 2004 and 2011, winning two World Series and leading the team to numerous playoff appearances, would take over as manager of the Indians starting with the 2013 season.<sup id="cite_ref-foxsports_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foxsports-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Indians entered the <a href="/wiki/2013_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="2013 Major League Baseball season">2013 season</a> following an active offseason that resulted in a dramatic roster turnover.  Key acquisitions included free agent 1B/OF <a href="/wiki/Nick_Swisher" title="Nick Swisher">Nick Swisher</a> and CF <a href="/wiki/Michael_Bourn" title="Michael Bourn">Michael Bourn</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rosenthal_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rosenthal-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> The Indians also added prized right handed pitching prospect <a href="/wiki/Trevor_Bauer" title="Trevor Bauer">Trevor Bauer</a>, OF <a href="/wiki/Drew_Stubbs" title="Drew Stubbs">Drew Stubbs</a>, and relief pitchers <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Shaw_(baseball)" title="Bryan Shaw (baseball)">Bryan Shaw</a> &amp;  <a href="/wiki/Matt_Albers" title="Matt Albers">Matt Albers</a> in a three-way trade with the <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Diamondbacks" title="Arizona Diamondbacks">Arizona Diamondbacks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Reds" title="Cincinnati Reds">Cincinnati Reds</a> that sent RF <a href="/wiki/Shin-Soo_Choo" title="Shin-Soo Choo">Shin-Soo Choo</a> to the Reds, and <a href="/wiki/Tony_Sipp" title="Tony Sipp">Tony Sipp</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Diamondbacks" title="Arizona Diamondbacks">Arizona Diamondbacks</a><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Other notable additions included utility man <a href="/wiki/Mike_Aviles" class="mw-redirect" title="Mike Aviles">Mike Aviles</a>, catcher <a href="/wiki/Yan_Gomes" title="Yan Gomes">Yan Gomes</a>, designated hitter <a href="/wiki/Jason_Giambi" title="Jason Giambi">Jason Giambi</a>, and starting pitcher <a href="/wiki/Scott_Kazmir" title="Scott Kazmir">Scott Kazmir</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rosenthal_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rosenthal-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hoynes_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hoynes-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>  The 2013 Indians were able to increase their win total by 24 over 2012 (from 68 to 92), finishing in second place behind Detroit by one game in the Central Division, and securing the number one seed in the American League Wild Card standings.  This marked the Indians\' first time in postseason play since 2007.  The 2013 season ended for the Indians on October 2, losing 4\xe2\x80\x930 to the <a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Rays" title="Tampa Bay Rays">Tampa Bay Rays</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2013_American_League_Wild_Card_Game" title="2013 American League Wild Card Game">2013 AL Wild Card Game</a>.  The turnaround from 2012 also led to Francona winning the 2013 <a href="/wiki/American_League_Manager_of_the_Year" class="mw-redirect" title="American League Manager of the Year">American League Manager of the Year</a> Award.\n</p><p>The Indians had their second consecutive winning season (not done since 2000\xe2\x80\x932001) in 2014 finishing 85\xe2\x80\x9377.  However, they finished third in the AL Central and missed the playoffs, having been eliminated from the AL Wild Card race during the last weekend of the season.\n</p><p>In 2015, after struggling through the first half of the season, the Indians finished 81-80 for their third consecutive winning season, which the team had not done since 1999\xe2\x80\x932001.  The Tribe finished third in the Central for the second straight year, and was eliminated from the Wild Card race during the last week of the season. Following the departure of longtime team executive <a href="/wiki/Mark_Shapiro_(sports_executive)" title="Mark Shapiro (sports executive)">Mark Shapiro</a> on October 6, the Indians promoted GM <a href="/wiki/Chris_Antonetti" title="Chris Antonetti">Chris Antonetti</a> to President of Baseball Operations, assistant general manager <a href="/wiki/Mike_Chernoff_(baseball)" title="Mike Chernoff (baseball)">Mike Chernoff</a> to GM, and named <a href="/wiki/Derek_Falvey" title="Derek Falvey">Derek Falvey</a> as assistant GM.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>  Falvey was later hired by the <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Twins" title="Minnesota Twins">Minnesota Twins</a> in 2016, becoming their President of Baseball Operations.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2016:_Return_to_the_World_Series">2016:  Return to the World Series</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cleveland_Indians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: 2016: Return to the World Series">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The Indians set what was then a franchise record for longest winning streak when they won their 14th consecutive game, a 2\xe2\x80\x931 win over the <a href="/wiki/2016_Toronto_Blue_Jays_season" title="2016 Toronto Blue Jays season">Toronto Blue Jays</a> in 19 innings on July 1, 2016 at <a href="/wiki/Rogers_Centre" title="Rogers Centre">Rogers Centre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> The team clinched the Central Division pennant on September 26, their eighth division title overall and first since 2007, as well as returning to the playoffs for the first time since 2013. They finished the regular season at 94\xe2\x80\x9367, marking their fourth straight winning season, a feat not accomplished since the 1990s and early 2000s.\n</p><p>The Indians began the 2016 postseason by sweeping the <a href="/wiki/2016_Boston_Red_Sox_season" title="2016 Boston Red Sox season">Boston Red Sox</a> in the best-of-five <a href="/wiki/2016_American_League_Division_Series" title="2016 American League Division Series">American League Division Series</a>. They then defeated the Blue Jays in five games in the <a href="/wiki/2016_American_League_Championship_Series" title="2016 American League Championship Series">2016 American League Championship Series</a> to claim their sixth American League pennant and advance to the <a href="/wiki/2016_World_Series" title="2016 World Series">World Series</a> against the <a href="/wiki/2016_Chicago_Cubs_season" title="2016 Chicago Cubs season">Chicago Cubs</a>. It marked the first appearance for the Indians in the World Series since 1997 and first for the Cubs since 1945. The Indians took a 3\xe2\x80\x931 series lead following a victory in Game 4 at <a href="/wiki/Wrigley_Field" title="Wrigley Field">Wrigley Field</a>, but the Cubs rallied to take the final three games and won the series 4 games to 3.  The Indians\' 2016 success led to Francona winning his second AL Manager of the Year Award with the club.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2017:_Record-setting_winning_streak">2017: Record-setting winning streak</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cleveland_Indians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: 2017: Record-setting winning streak">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>From August 24 through September 15 during the 2017 season, the Indians set a new American League record by winning 22 games in a row.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> On September 28, the Indians won their 100th game of the season, marking only the third time in history the team has reached that milestone. They finished the regular season with 102 wins, second most in team history (behind 1954\'s 111 win team). The Indians earned the AL Central Title for the second consecutive year, along with home-field advantage throughout the American League playoffs, but they lost the <a href="/wiki/2017_ALDS" class="mw-redirect" title="2017 ALDS">2017 ALDS</a> to the <a href="/wiki/2017_New_York_Yankees_season" title="2017 New York Yankees season">Yankees</a> 3\xe2\x80\x932 after being up 2\xe2\x80\x930.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Season-by-season_results">Season-by-season results</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cleveland_Indians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Season-by-season results">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Cleveland_Indians_seasons" title="List of Cleveland Indians seasons">List of Cleveland Indians seasons</a></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries">Rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cleveland_Indians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Rivalries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Interleague">Interleague</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cleveland_Indians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Interleague">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Cup" title="Ohio Cup">Ohio Cup</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ohio_Cup_Trophy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fa/Ohio_Cup_Trophy.jpg/220px-Ohio_Cup_Trophy.jpg" width="220" height="324" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fa/Ohio_Cup_Trophy.jpg/330px-Ohio_Cup_Trophy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fa/Ohio_Cup_Trophy.jpg/440px-Ohio_Cup_Trophy.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1900" data-file-height="2800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ohio_Cup_Trophy.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Ohio Cup trophy</div></div></div>\n<p>The rivalry with fellow <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">Ohio</a> team the <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Reds" title="Cincinnati Reds">Cincinnati Reds</a> is known as the Battle of Ohio or Buckeye Series and features the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Cup" title="Ohio Cup">Ohio Cup</a> trophy for the winner. Prior to 1997, the winner of the cup was determined by an annual <a href="/wiki/Spring_training" title="Spring training">pre-season</a> baseball game, played each year at minor-league <a href="/wiki/Cooper_Stadium" title="Cooper Stadium">Cooper Stadium</a> in the state capital of <a href="/wiki/Columbus,_Ohio" title="Columbus, Ohio">Columbus</a>, and staged just days before the start of each new <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> season. A total of eight Ohio Cup games were played, with the Indians winning six of them. It ended with the start of <a href="/wiki/Interleague_play" title="Interleague play">interleague play</a> in 1997. The winner of the game each year was awarded the Ohio Cup in postgame ceremonies. The Ohio Cup was a favorite among baseball fans in Columbus, with attendances regularly topping 15,000.\n</p><p>Since 1997, the two teams have played each other as part of the regular season, with the exception of 2002. The Ohio Cup was reintroduced in 2008 and is presented to the team who wins the most games in the series that season. Initially, the teams only played one three-game series per season, meeting in Cleveland in 1997 and Cincinnati the following year. Since 1999, the teams have played two series per season against each other, one series at each ballpark. Since 2013, each series is two games, except in years where the AL Central plays the NL Central in interleague play, when the teams play two three-game series.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Through the 2018 meetings, the Indians lead the series 60\xe2\x80\x9349.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Divisional">Divisional</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cleveland_Indians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Divisional">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>As the Indians play 19 games every year with each of their AL Central competitors, several rivalries have developed.\n</p><p>The Indians have a rivalry with the <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Tigers" title="Detroit Tigers">Detroit Tigers</a> due to the fact that the two cities are fairly close to each other, the teams have been battling for the AL Central championship in recent years, and has some carryover elements from the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State-Michigan_rivalry" class="mw-redirect" title="Ohio State-Michigan rivalry">Ohio State-Michigan rivalry</a>, as well as the general historic rivalry between Michigan and Ohio dating back to the <a href="/wiki/Toledo_War" title="Toledo War">Toledo War</a>. \n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Chicago_White_Sox" title="Chicago White Sox">Chicago White Sox</a> are another rival, dating back to the 1959 season, when the Sox slipped past the Tribe to win the AL pennant. The rivalry intensified when both clubs were moved to the new AL Central in 1994.  During the 1994 season, the two teams challenged for the division title, with the Indians one game back of Chicago when the strike began in August. During a game in Chicago, the White Sox confiscated <a href="/wiki/Albert_Belle" title="Albert Belle">Albert Belle</a>\'s corked bat, followed by an attempt by Indians pitcher <a href="/wiki/Jason_Grimsley" title="Jason Grimsley">Jason Grimsley</a> to crawl through the <a href="/wiki/Comiskey_Park_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Comiskey Park II">Comiskey Park</a> clubhouse ceiling to retrieve it. Belle later signed with the White Sox in 1997, adding additional intensity to the rivalry.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Logos_and_uniforms">Logos and uniforms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cleveland_Indians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Logos and uniforms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<dl><dd><i>See also: <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_uniforms" title="Major League Baseball uniforms">Major League Baseball uniforms</a></i></dd></dl>\n<p>The Cleveland Indians\' official team colors are red, navy blue, and white.<sup id="cite_ref-IndiansUniformPlan_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IndiansUniformPlan-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The team\'s home uniform is white with navy piping around each sleeve. Across the front of the jersey in script font is the word "Indians" in red with a navy outline. The jersey has the Chief Wahoo logo on the left sleeve, with red undershirts, belts, and socks.  The standard home cap is navy with a red bill and features the Chief Wahoo logo on the front. \n</p><p>The road uniform is gray, with "Cleveland" in navy block letters trimmed in red is across the front of the jersey, navy piping around the sleeves, and the Chief Wahoo logo located on the left sleeve, with navy undershirts, belts, and socks. The standard road cap is navy, with a red block "C" on the front.\n</p><p>The universal alternate third jersey is <a href="/wiki/Navy_blue" title="Navy blue">navy blue</a> with white piping around each sleeve. Script "Indians" is located across the front of the jersey in the same fashion as the home uniform (red lettering with a white outline); the Chief Wahoo logo is on the left sleeve.  \n</p><p>The team also has alternate caps - navy with the Chief Wahoo logo for road games, and red with a navy block "C" for home games.<sup id="cite_ref-IndiansUniformPlan_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IndiansUniformPlan-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>For all games, the team uses a navy batting helmet with a red block "C" on the front.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fan_support_and_traditions">Fan support and traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cleveland_Indians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Fan support and traditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Drummer">The Drummer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cleveland_Indians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: The Drummer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Adams_drummer.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/John_Adams_drummer.jpg/170px-John_Adams_drummer.jpg" width="170" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/John_Adams_drummer.jpg/255px-John_Adams_drummer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/John_Adams_drummer.jpg/340px-John_Adams_drummer.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1634" data-file-height="1444" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Adams_drummer.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/John_Adams_(drummer)" title="John Adams (drummer)">John Adams</a> \xe2\x80\x93 who (along with his drum) has been an iconic fixture at Indians home games for over 40 years.</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/John_Adams_(drummer)" title="John Adams (drummer)">John Adams (drummer)</a></div>\n<p>John Adams, known by baseball fans as "The Drummer", has played a <a href="/wiki/Bass_drum" title="Bass drum">bass drum</a> at nearly every home game since 1973. He is the only fan for whom the team has dedicated a <a href="/wiki/Bobble_head" class="mw-redirect" title="Bobble head">bobble head</a> day.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Adams originally paid for his tickets (one for himself, and one for his drum), but recently the Indians have paid for his seats in honor of the contributions he has made to the ballpark atmosphere. He has been featured and interviewed on national TV shows and newspaper articles.\n<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sellout_streak">Sellout streak</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cleveland_Indians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Sellout streak">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Between June 12, 1995 and April 4, 2001, the Indians sold out 455 consecutive home games, drawing a total of 19,324,248 fans to <a href="/wiki/Jacobs_Field" class="mw-redirect" title="Jacobs Field">Jacobs Field</a>. The demand for tickets was so great that all 81 home games were sold out before <a href="/wiki/Opening_Day" title="Opening Day">Opening Day</a> on at least three separate occasions. The sellout streak set a Major League Baseball record; this was broken by the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a> on September 8, 2008, though Boston\'s <a href="/wiki/Fenway_Park" title="Fenway Park">Fenway Park</a> is considerably smaller than Progressive Field.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> One night after the streak ended, the Indians honored the fans by retiring the number 455.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Signature_songs">Signature songs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cleveland_Indians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Signature songs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Indians play "<a href="/wiki/Hang_On_Sloopy" title="Hang On Sloopy">Hang On Sloopy</a>" by <a href="/wiki/The_McCoys" title="The McCoys">The McCoys</a> during the middle of the 8th inning, bringing with it the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_Buckeyes" title="Ohio State Buckeyes">Ohio State Buckeyes</a>\' tradition of the fans chanting "O-H-I-O" during the chorus. They also play "<a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Rocks" title="Cleveland Rocks">Cleveland Rocks</a>" at the end of the game for Indians wins.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Nickname_and_logo_controversy">Nickname and logo controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cleveland_Indians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Nickname and logo controversy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians_name_and_logo_controversy" title="Cleveland Indians name and logo controversy">Cleveland Indians name and logo controversy</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Native_American_mascot_controversy" title="Native American mascot controversy">Native American mascot controversy</a></div>\n<p>The club nickname and its cartoon logo have been criticized for perpetuating Native American stereotypes. In 1997 and 1998, protesters were arrested after effigies were burned. Charges were dismissed in the 1997 case, and were not filed in the 1998 case. Protesters arrested in the 1998 incident subsequently fought and lost a lawsuit alleging that their <a href="/wiki/First_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="First Amendment to the United States Constitution">First Amendment</a> rights had been violated.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-OSSC_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OSSC-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Bud_Selig" title="Bud Selig">Bud Selig</a> (then-<a href="/wiki/Commissioner_of_Baseball" title="Commissioner of Baseball">Commissioner of Baseball</a>) said in 2014 that he had never received a complaint about the logo. He has heard that there are some protesting mascots, but individual teams such as the Indians and <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Braves" title="Atlanta Braves">Atlanta Braves</a>, whose nickname was also criticized for similar reasons, should make their own decisions.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> Native Americans protested <a href="/wiki/Chief_Wahoo" title="Chief Wahoo">Chief Wahoo</a> on <a href="/wiki/Opening_Day" title="Opening Day">Opening Day</a> 2015, as they have for many years, making note that this is the 100th anniversary of the team becoming the Indians. Owner <a href="/wiki/Paul_Dolan_(baseball)" title="Paul Dolan (baseball)">Paul Dolan</a>, while stating he is respectful of critics, says he mainly hears from fans who want to keep Chief Wahoo, and has no plans to change.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On January 29, 2018, Major League Baseball announced that Chief Wahoo will be removed from the Indians\' uniforms as of the 2019 season, stating that the logo was no longer appropriate for on-field use.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> The team will consider a new logo in the future, but the block "C" will be promoted to the primary logo; additionally, there are no plans to change the team\'s name.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cleveland_Indians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Cleveland_Indians_broadcasters" title="List of Cleveland Indians broadcasters">List of Cleveland Indians broadcasters</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians_Radio_Network" title="Cleveland Indians Radio Network">Cleveland Indians Radio Network</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Indians TV announcer <a href="/wiki/Matt_Underwood" title="Matt Underwood">Matt Underwood</a> (seated, center) and longtime lead radio announcer <a href="/wiki/Tom_Hamilton_(broadcaster)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tom Hamilton (broadcaster)">Tom Hamilton</a> (right)</div></div></div>\n<p>The Indians\' flagship radio stations are <a href="/wiki/WTAM" title="WTAM">WTAM</a> AM 1100 and <a href="/wiki/WMMS" title="WMMS">WMMS</a> FM 100.7.<sup id="cite_ref-radio_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-radio-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> The broadcast team consists of longtime "Voice of the Tribe" and seven-time <a href="/wiki/National_Sportscasters_and_Sportswriters_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="National Sportscasters and Sportswriters Association">NSSA</a> Ohio Sportscaster of the Year <a href="/wiki/Tom_Hamilton_(broadcaster)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tom Hamilton (broadcaster)">Tom Hamilton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jim_Rosenhaus" title="Jim Rosenhaus">Jim Rosenhaus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-broadcasters_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-broadcasters-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The television rights are held by the <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_(United_States)" title="Fox Sports (United States)">Fox Sports</a> owned <a href="/wiki/SportsTime_Ohio" title="SportsTime Ohio">SportsTime Ohio</a> (STO), a network launched in <a href="/wiki/2006_in_baseball" title="2006 in baseball">2006</a> by the Indians, and purchased by Fox in 2012. <a href="/wiki/Matt_Underwood" title="Matt Underwood">Matt Underwood</a> and former Indians <a href="/wiki/Gold_Glove" class="mw-redirect" title="Gold Glove">Gold Glove</a> winning CF <a href="/wiki/Rick_Manning" title="Rick Manning">Rick Manning</a> form the announcing team,<sup id="cite_ref-broadcasters_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-broadcasters-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>  with veteran Cleveland sportscaster Andre Knott as field reporter,<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Al_Pawlowski" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Pawlowski">Al Pawlowski</a> and former Indians pitcher <a href="/wiki/Jensen_Lewis" title="Jensen Lewis">Jensen Lewis</a> as pregame/postgame hosts.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>  Select games are shown on free TV, airing on <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a> affiliate <a href="/wiki/WKYC" title="WKYC">WKYC</a> channel 3 via simulcast.\n</p><p>Notable former Indians broadcasters include Tom Manning, <a href="/wiki/Jack_Graney" title="Jack Graney">Jack Graney</a> (the first ex-baseball player to become a play-by-play announcer), <a href="/wiki/Ken_Coleman" title="Ken Coleman">Ken Coleman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Castiglione" title="Joe Castiglione">Joe Castiglione</a>, <a href="/wiki/Van_Patrick" title="Van Patrick">Van Patrick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nev_Chandler" title="Nev Chandler">Nev Chandler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Drennan" title="Bruce Drennan">Bruce Drennan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mudcat_Grant" title="Mudcat Grant">Jim "Mudcat" Grant</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Colavito" title="Rocky Colavito">Rocky Colavito</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dan_Coughlin_(sportscaster)" title="Dan Coughlin (sportscaster)">Dan Coughlin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jim_Donovan_(sportscaster)" title="Jim Donovan (sportscaster)">Jim Donovan</a>.\n</p><p>Previous broadcasters who have had lengthy tenures with the team include <a href="/wiki/Joe_Tait" title="Joe Tait">Joe Tait</a> (15 seasons between TV and radio), <a href="/wiki/Jack_Corrigan_(radio)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jack Corrigan (radio)">Jack Corrigan</a> (18 seasons on TV), <a href="/wiki/Ford_C._Frick_Award" title="Ford C. Frick Award">Ford C. Frick Award</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Dudley" title="Jimmy Dudley">Jimmy Dudley</a> (19 seasons on radio), <a href="/wiki/Mike_Hegan" title="Mike Hegan">Mike Hegan</a> (23 seasons between TV and radio), and <a href="/wiki/Herb_Score" title="Herb Score">Herb Score</a> (34 seasons between TV and radio).<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cleveland_Indians_in_popular_culture">Cleveland Indians in popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cleveland_Indians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Cleveland Indians in popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Indians over the years have been featured in numerous movies and television shows.  Examples include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Kid_From_Cleveland" class="mw-redirect" title="The Kid From Cleveland">The Kid From Cleveland</a></i> \xe2\x80\x93 a 1949 film featuring then owner Bill Veeck and numerous players from the team (coming off winning the <a href="/wiki/1948_World_Series" title="1948 World Series">1948 World Series</a>).</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Major_League_(film)" title="Major League (film)">Major League</a></i> \xe2\x80\x93 a 1989 film centered around a fictionalized version of the team</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Major_League_II" title="Major League II">Major League II</a></i> \xe2\x80\x93 a 1994 sequel to the original from five years earlier</li>\n<li>In the 1994 film <i><a href="/wiki/Little_Big_League" title="Little Big League">Little Big League</a></i>, the main character Billy Heywood quotes Indians\' Hall-of-Fame pitcher <a href="/wiki/Bob_Lemon" title="Bob Lemon">Bob Lemon</a>: "Baseball was made for kids; grownups only screw it up."<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> In addition, catcher <a href="/wiki/Sandy_Alomar_Jr." title="Sandy Alomar Jr.">Sandy Alomar Jr.</a> and second baseman <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Baerga" title="Carlos Baerga">Carlos Baerga</a> have cameo appearances.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>In an episode from the 1968 animated series <i><a href="/wiki/Go_Go_Gophers" title="Go Go Gophers">Go Go Gophers</a></i> titled "The Cleveland Indians", Indian characters Ruffled Feathers and Running Board not only accused the team of not being real Indians and not wearing any feathers, but also called them fakes.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>In the children\'s book <i><a href="/wiki/Danny_Dunn,_Time_Traveler" title="Danny Dunn, Time Traveler">Danny Dunn, Time Traveler</a></i>, when they are sitting around with Benjamin Franklin and explaining their presence in 1763, Danny\'s role model, a professor, is unable to name any Indian tribe as the one they claimed had captured them.  The professor named the only Indian "tribe" he could think of: the Cleveland Indians.</li>\n<li>In an episode of <a href="/wiki/I_Love_Lucy" title="I Love Lucy">I Love Lucy</a> ("Lucy and Bob Hope") Lucy spots <a href="/wiki/Bob_Hope" title="Bob Hope">Bob Hope</a> at an Indians-Yankees Game in <a href="/wiki/Yankee_Stadium" title="Yankee Stadium">Yankee Stadium</a> (At the time, Bob Hope was a minority owner of The Indians) and tries to talk to him into appearing with her husband Ricky at the Grand Opening of Club Babalu while disguised as a Hot Dog Vendor then an Indians Player.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_honors">Awards and honors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cleveland_Indians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Awards and honors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians_award_winners_and_league_leaders" title="Cleveland Indians award winners and league leaders">Cleveland Indians href="/w/index.php?title=Cleveland_Indians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Indians Hall of Fame">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians_award_winners_and_league_leaders#Cleveland_Indians_Hall_of_Fame" title="Cleveland Indians award winners and league leaders">Cleveland Indians award winners and league leaders \xc2\xa7&#160;Cleveland Indians Hall of Fame</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Statues">Statues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cleveland_Indians&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Statues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Indians players who have had statues made in their honor in and around Progressive Field include:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Bob_Feller" title="Bob Feller">Bob Feller</a> (Indians all-time leader in wins and strikeouts by a pitcher, <a href="/wiki/1948_World_Series" title="1948 World Series">1948 World Series</a> Champion, eight-time All-Star) \xe2\x80\x93 since 1994*</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jim_Thome" title="Jim Thome">Jim Thome</a> (Indians all-time leader in home runs and walks by a hitter, three-time All-Star with the Indians) \xe2\x80\x93 since 2014*</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Larry_Doby" title="Larry Doby">Larry Doby</a> (First black player in the American League, <a href="/wiki/1948_World_Series" title="1948 World Series">1948 World Series</a> Champion, seven-time All-Star) \xe2\x80\x93 since 2015*</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Frank_Robinson" title="Frank Robinson">Frank Robinson</a> (Became first black manager in MLB history when he served as player/manager for the Indians from 1975-1977) \xe2\x80\x93 since 2017</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lou_Boudreau" title="Lou Boudreau">Lou Boudreau</a> (1948 AL MVP, <a href="/wiki/1948_World_Series" title="1948 World Series">1948 World Series</a> Champion as player/manager, eight-time All-Star) \xe2\x80\x93 since 2017*<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>(*) - Inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Baseball_Hall_of_Fame" class="mw-redirect" title="Baseball Hall of Fame">Baseball Hall of Fame</a> as an Indian.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Franchise_records">Franchise records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span
